EARTHWORK OBSERVATION AND COMPACTION TESTING REPORT 
MASS AND PAD GRADING 
GENTRY KALAELOA PARCEL 1 
RESIDENTIAL DEVELOPMENT PHASE 1 
KALAELOA, OAHU, HAWAII 
TMK NO.:  9-1-013:  PORS. 197 AND 199 
GRADING PERMIT NO. GP2023-01-0006 
Dear Mr. Maja: 
This report summarizes our geotechnical engineering observation and compaction 
testing services performed during mass and pad grading for the Gentry Kalaeloa Parcel 1, 
Residential Development Phase 1 project from December 6, 2022 to January 5, 2024 in 
accordance with our fee proposals dated December 19, 2022 and September 15, 2023. 
PROJECT CONSIDERATIONS 
The proposed Gentry Kalaeloa Development is located near the intersection of 
Kamokila Boulevard and Roosevelt Avenue in Kalaeloa on the Island of Oahu, Hawaii. 
The property encompasses an area of approximately 31 acres. The project site is located 
at the northeast corner of the property.  A Project Location Map and Site Plans are shown 
on Plates 1 and 2.1 through 2.4, respectively. 
The project involves mass and pad grading for a residential development consisting 
of single-family units of multi-family, two-story six-plex and 8-plex buildings with 
slabs-on-grade and related access roads.  The mass grading work involved fills up to 
about 5 feet and cuts up to about 2 feet to achieve the finished grades.  In addition, the 
project includes roadway construction. 
This report addresses our field observations and compaction testing services for 
the mass and pad grading and roadway construction at the project site. 
Gentry Homes, Limited 
Page 2 
W.O. 8282-10 
February 9, 2024 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California 
MASS AND PAD GRADING AND ROADWAY CONSTRUCTION 
We observed the mass and pad grading and roadway construction work for the 
Gentry 
Kalaeloa 
Parcel 
1, 
Residential 
Development 
Phase 
1 
project 
from 
December 6, 2022 to January 5, 2024. The mass and pad grading work consisted of 
placement and compaction of fills up to about 5 feet thick to achieve the finished grades 
for the project.  The mass and pad grading work were performed by Royal Contracting 
Company Ltd. During the mass and pad grading operations, we obtained samples of the 
on-site and imported materials utilized as fill and backfill materials and transported them to 
our laboratory for testing. The maximum dry densities and optimum moisture contents 
were established in our laboratory in general accordance with ASTM D1557 (Modified 
Proctor), and the test results are summarized on Plate 3. 
The fill and backfill materials were moisture-conditioned to above the optimum 
moisture content and compacted to a minimum of 90 percent of the maximum dry density 
as determined in accordance with ASTM D1557.  In the roadway areas, the fill and backfill 
materials within 2 feet of the finished subgrade were compacted to a minimum of 
95 percent relative density. 
During the mass and pad grading and roadway construction, periodic field density 
tests were performed in general accordance with ASTM D6938 (Nuclear Gauge Method). 
Results of the compaction tests performed are summarized on Plates 4.1 through 4.92 of 
this report. These tests were performed on the prepared ground surfaces and on 
constructed fills and backfills at the site. Test locations and elevations were estimated by 
pacing and interpolating from on-site survey stakes. These locations and elevations should 
be considered accurate only to the degree implied by the methods used. Areas assessed 
as unsatisfactory were reworked until the specified minimum compaction was obtained 
and/or approved by our field representative based on visual observation and hand probing. 
Our services consisted of part-time field observation of the contractor’s fill 
placement, subgrade preparation, compaction procedures, and confirmation of subgrade 
soil conditions exposed during the above grading operations. 
Based on the observations of our field representatives and the results of the 
referenced tests, it is our opinion that the mass and pad grading and roadway construction 
for the above-referenced project observed and tested by Geolabs in the period covered by 
this report were performed in conformance with the general intent of the recommendations 
in the following references. 
1. 
Chapter 14 of the Revised Ordinances of Honolulu 1990, as amended. 
2. 
Report by Geolabs, Inc. entitled “Geotechnical Engineering Study, Gentry 
Kalaeloa Development, Kalaeloa, Oahu, Hawaii," dated June 2, 2021. 
Gentry Homes, Limited Page 3
W.O. 8282-10
February 9, 2024
LIMITATIONS
Geolabs assumes no responsibility for any alterations made to the slopes or
finished grades on the above project subsequent to our observation and testing period
without our knowledge and written acknowledgment.
It should be noted that it is not possible to continuously observe all activities
occurring simultaneously on a construction site; therefore, some work may have occurred
without our observation. However, we believe that the level of earthwork observation and
testing services provided is reasonable in reducing the geotechnical risks to the project. It
should be recognized that there are variations in the accuracy and statistical repeatability
of the tests and methods used to monitor earthwork construction and materials. Our
services were performed in accordance with generally accepted standards of geotechnical
engineering practice; no warranty is expressed or implied. The provision of construction
monitoring by an engineer is not insurance, nor does it guarantee construction of any type.
The contractor shall retain responsibility for the quality of the work, for adhering to the
plans and specifications, and for repairing defects regardless of when they are found.
CLOSURE
We appreciate the opportunity to be of service to you on this project. If you have
questions or need additional information, please contact our office.
Respectfully submitted,
GEOLABS, INC.
